<div id="review_1365180929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365180929" />
    <a title="Tarmia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46015060-tarmia"><img alt="Tarmia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495543944p2/46015060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365180929?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tarmia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tarmia" href="/user/show/46015060-tarmia">Tarmia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407143620" href="/book/show/35665263-the-railway-children">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=adolescent-fiction">adolescent-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=classical-literature">classical-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=reading-challenge-2017">reading-challenge-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365180929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5649850720769662729">This was an endearing read, but one that, for me, was nothing more than endearing. The children, the side characters, and the narrator were all well considered and gave an almost whimsical sensation to the book, but I was lost when trying to properly connect and feel emotionally invested. It was very reminiscent of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_' title='Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Women</a> but luckily had less of the sexist undertones. Yes, I am aware of when these books were written, but I felt almost 'dirtied' by such statements as; 'girls are so much sof</span>
  <span id="freeText5649850720769662729" style="display:none">This was an endearing read, but one that, for me, was nothing more than endearing. The children, the side characters, and the narrator were all well considered and gave an almost whimsical sensation to the book, but I was lost when trying to properly connect and feel emotionally invested. It was very reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_" title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Women</a> but luckily had less of the sexist undertones. Yes, I am aware of when these books were written, but I felt almost 'dirtied' by such statements as; 'girls are so much softer and weaker than we are; they have to be, you know'. With both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/164531.The_Railway_Children" title="The Railway Children by E. Nesbit" rel="nofollow noopener">The Railway Children</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_" title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Women</a> I think it's the childhood sentimentality that I am missing; neither of these books were read to me as a child, and this is where they fall short. While reading this I was not transported back to my childhood bedroom but to a time where it was acceptable to indoctrinate children with the stereotypes of boys being 'brave warriors' and girls being 'gentle and kind' and the opposite not being accepted. <b> I know</b> this is a children's book, and that much of this would go beyond their understanding, however, I struggle to get past this and to fully enjoy the adventures of the children. I wish I had read this as a child, then maybe I would like it more, see the adventure, the beauty in the countryside setting, and feel the pain of the children when their father disappears. But I struggle to move on from the misogyny that is so innocently presented. I would have loved to have viewed this endearing story through the innocent eyes of a child and to fully appreciate it for what it is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5649850720769662729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2116036969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2116036969" />
    <a title="Marlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27110787-marlene"><img alt="Marlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464639719p2/27110787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2116036969?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marlene" href="/user/show/27110787-marlene">Marlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27110787-marlene?shelf=own-kindle">own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27110787-marlene?shelf=also-for-nora">also-for-nora</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27110787-marlene?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2116036969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15255899851009752199">"...it's not so much what you do, as what you mean." <br/><br/><i>The Railway Children</i> (1906, Wells Gardner, Darton) by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7935185.E__Nesbit' title='E. Nesbit' rel='nofollow noopener'> E. Nesbit</a>, is a children's chapter book set in Edwardian England near a railway station in Yorkshire. According to Wikipedia, the timeframe is thought to be the year 1905, which is the same year this story was published serially in <i>The London Magazine</i>. I tend to enjoy classic children's books, so when I found this title in my husband's library of Audible books, how could I resist?<br/><br/><b>Rating: 5</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15255899851009752199" style="display:none">"...it's not so much what you do, as what you mean." <br /><br /><i>The Railway Children</i> (1906, Wells Gardner, Darton) by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7935185.E__Nesbit" title="E. Nesbit" rel="nofollow noopener"> E. Nesbit</a>, is a children's chapter book set in Edwardian England near a railway station in Yorkshire. According to Wikipedia, the timeframe is thought to be the year 1905, which is the same year this story was published serially in <i>The London Magazine</i>. I tend to enjoy classic children's books, so when I found this title in my husband's library of Audible books, how could I resist?<br /><br /><b>Rating: 5 stars</b><br /><b>Narration: 5 stars</b><br /><br /><b>The plot:</b> Roberta (8), Peter (10), Phyllis (12), and their mother are uprooted from their London home to live in a country house in Yorkshire called <i>The Three Chimneys.</i> The children's father has had to leave due to some unspecified problem, and they are now experiencing financial difficulties. (In the book, the reveal for what precipitated their father's departure comes quite late in the story, so it may be wise not to read plot summaries. There are no spoilers in this review.) The children miss their father, but adapt well, and in their new home they quickly grow to love the railway nearby. They form a strong connection with everything about the railway and the people associated with it. <br /><br />I enjoyed the story so much that I put a movie adaptation on my wish list!<br /><br /><b>Christian elements:</b><br /><br />"Don't you think it's rather nice to think that we're in a book that God's writing? If I were writing the book, I might make mistakes. But God knows how to make the story end just right—in the way that's best for us." It reminds me of the following Bible verse: "And we know that God causes everything to work together for the good of those who love God and are called according to his purpose for them." (Romans 8:28)<br /><br />This isn't a work of Christian fiction by any means, but I appreciated that the morals portrayed in this story are very good. When anyone is in the wrong, it is addressed at some point rather than being ignored, justified, or glorified. <br /><br /><b>Is it clean/chaste?</b> Yes, certainly. <br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b> <br /><br />*"Girls are just as clever as boys, and don't you forget it!" Phyllis and her mother are both admirably strong characters.<br /><br />*The children's characters are so very authentic. I loved them. The secondary characters are fantastic as well.<br /><br />*The children's mother is quite the poet and storyteller. I can't help but wonder whether she is fashioned after the author. <br /><br /><b>What I didn’t like:</b> <br /><br />*There are too many coincidences for this story to be plausible. However, I didn't feel that way until I was nearly at the end, and I think implausibility is more forgivable in a children's story, anyway. <br /><br />*I read the short biography about Ms. Nesbit on GR, and what a sad tale it is! I cannot imagine living under those conditions - what strength it would require to withstand such a life. My heart hurts for this woman who lived one hundred years ago. <br /><br /><b>Audiobook:</b> The narrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2265435.Virginia_Leishman?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">(Virginia Leishman)</a> was rather wonderful. This was my first time reading this book, and yet the audio version was easy for me to understand! (I'm deaf, and up until this point have only listened to books I've previously read via hard copy in order to increase my chances of understanding the narrator.)<br /><br />***********<br /><br /><b>The bottom line:</b> This was a lovely story of the adventures of three close-knit siblings in Edwardian England. I recommend this book to any lover of classic children's literature. I look forward to reading more by this author, and plan to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/444374.The_Story_of_the_Treasure_Seekers__Bastable_Children___1_" title="The Story of the Treasure Seekers (Bastable Children, #1) by E. Nesbit" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Story of the Treasure Seekers</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15255899851009752199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VdSjIAYG1/E1XmTJaEbLW5ZeEpIjCpoSP0EPRPCXzbKUjX4nWdD4Hl1cEujh2kW1Z4hyHIQQLJvfRyuwW29GSw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S8+9C7Vlg4Ok3zK4su5UBWbf03wov8H/FutBLLetx8WKlmAM6rOsbMzdRJk7ctrrlwmz8o+ld3b27WXYHFVMPA==')})
  }

How this resourceful girl\'s fortunes change again is at the center of A Little Princess, one of the best-loved stories in all of children\'s literature. This unique and fully annotated edition appends excerpts from Frances Hodgson Burnett\'s original 1888 novella Sara Crewe and the stage play that preceded the novel, as well as an early story, &quot;Behind the White Brick,&quot; allowing readers to see how A Little Princess evolved. Initially pub<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11115496147672802326\" style=\"display:none\">&quot;One of the most delightful and enduring classics of children\'s literature, The Secret Garden by Victorian author Frances Hodgson Burnett has remained a firm favorite with children the world over ever since it made its first appearance. Initially published as a serial story in 1910 in The American Magazine, it was brought out in novel form in 1911.  The plot centers round Mary Lennox, a young English girl who returns to England from India, having suffered the immense trauma by losing both her parents in a cholera epidemic. However, her memories of her parents are not pleasant, as they were a selfish, neglectful and pleasure-seeking couple. Mary is given to the care of her uncle Archibald Craven, whom she has never met. She travels to his home, Misselthwaite Manor located in the gloomy Yorkshire, a vast change from the sunny and warm climate she was used to. When she arrives, she is a rude, stubborn and given to stormy temper tantrums. However, her nature undergoes a gradual transformation when she learns of the tragedies that have befallen her strict and disciplinarian uncle whom she earlier feared and despised. Once when he\'s away from home, Mary discovers a charming walled garden which is always kept locked. The mystery deepens when she hears sounds of sobbing from somewhere within her uncle\'s vast mansion. The kindly servants ignore her queries or pretend they haven\'t heard, spiking Mary\'s curiosity.  The Secret Garden appeals to both young and old alike. It has wonderful elements of mystery, spirituality, charming characters and an authentic rendering of childhood emotions and experiences. Commonsense, truth and kindness, compassion and a belief in the essential goodness of human beings lie at the heart of this unforgettable story. It is the best known of Frances Hodgson Burnett\'s works, though most of us have definitely heard of, if not read, her other novel Little Lord Fauntleroy.  The book has been adapted extensively on stage, film and television and translated into all the world\'s major languages. In 1991, a Japanese anime version was launched for television in Japan. It remains a popular and beloved story of a child\'s journey into maturity, and a must-read for every child, parent, teacher and anyone who would enjoy this fascinating glimpse of childhood. One of the most delightful and enduring classics of children\'s literature, The Secret Garden by Victorian author Frances Hodgson Burnett has remained a firm favorite with children the world over ever since it made its first appearance. Initially published as a serial story in 1910 in The American Magazine, it was brought out in novel form in 1911.&quot; <\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11115496147672802326\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7935185.E_Nesbit">About E. Nesbit</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7935185.E_Nesbit"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1395657856p3/7935185.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1829693938171495488">Edith Nesbit (married name Edith Bland; 15 August 1858 – 4 May 1924) was an English author and poet; she published her books for children under the name of E. Nesbit.<br/>She wrote or collaborated on over 60 books of fiction for children, several of which have been adapted for film and television. She was also a political activist and co-founded the Fabian Society, a socialist organisation later connec</span>
  <span id="freeText1829693938171495488" style="display:none">Edith Nesbit (married name Edith Bland; 15 August 1858 – 4 May 1924) was an English author and poet; she published her books for children under the name of E. Nesbit.<br />She wrote or collaborated on over 60 books of fiction for children, several of which have been adapted for film and television. She was also a political activist and co-founded the Fabian Society, a socialist organisation later connected to the Labour Party.<br /><br />Edith Nesbit was born in Kennington, Surrey, the daughter of agricultural chemist and schoolmaster John Collis Nesbit. The death of her father when she was four and the continuing ill health of her sister meant that Nesbit had a transitory childhood, her family moving across Europe in search of healthy climates only to return to England for financial reasons. Nesbit therefore spent her childhood attaining an education from whatever sources were available—local grammars, the occasional boarding school but mainly through reading.<br /><br />At 17 her family finally settled in London and aged 19, Nesbit met Hubert Bland, a political activist and writer. They became lovers and when Nesbit found she was pregnant they became engaged, marrying in April 1880. After this scandalous (for Victorian society) beginning, the marriage would be an unconventional one. Initially, the couple lived separately—Nesbit with her family and Bland with his mother and her live-in companion Maggie Doran.<br /><br />Initially, Edith Nesbit books were novels meant for adults, including <i>The Prophet's Mantle</i> (1885) and <i>The Marden Mystery</i> (1896) about the early days of the socialist movement. Written under the pen name of her third child 'Fabian Bland', these books were not successful. Nesbit generated an income for the family by lecturing around the country on socialism and through her journalism (she was editor of the Fabian Society's journal, <i>Today</i>).<br /><br />In 1899 she had published <i>The Adventures of the Treasure Seekers</i> to great acclaim.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1829693938171495488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2880113-the-railway-children">Quotes from The Railway Children</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Also she had the power of silent sympathy. That sounds rather dull, I know, but it's not so dull as it sounds. It just means that a person is able to know that you are unhappy, and to love you extra on that account, without bothering you by telling you all the time how sorry she is for you.&rdquo;</span>
